34
false
Joined the U.S. Army in 1818 and served under Andrew Jackson, a hero of the War of 1812, as a 2nd lieutenant in the 1st U.S. Infantry. In June 1834 he beat a female slave to death with a cane, but was acquitted in 1835. Fought in the Indian Wars and the Mexican War, where he commanded the 2nd Dragoons, but was replaced due to bad temper, but continued in the war and was brevetted a brigadier general.

35
false
In 1836 moved to Texas to participate in its war for independence against Mexico. Briefly served as a Texas Ranger. In 1846 joined the First Regiment, Texas Mounted Riflemen, as a first lieutenant to fight in the Mexican War. Fought with honors at the Battle of Monterey and was given the rank of major and command of his own battalion.

false
A Mexican militiaman since 1837, receiving the cross of honor from the Mexican government for negotiating the surrender of about half of the Texas Santa Fe Expedition in 1841. Joined the U.S. military in 1847 after Sante Fe was surrendered in the Mexican War. Fought the Indians in U.S. militia.
